id="cite_ref-cassel68_173-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cassel68-173">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> It is alleged by many, including members of the security forces, that Jackson was an RUC agent.<sup id="cite_ref-cassel68_173-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cassel68-173">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> The Irish Government\'s <i>Barron Report</i> alleged that he also "had relationships with British Intelligence".<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Smithwick_Tribunal" title="Smithwick Tribunal">Smithwick Tribunal</a> also concluded that a member of the <a href="/wiki/Garda_S%C3%ADoch%C3%A1na" title="Garda S\xc3\xadoch\xc3\xa1na">Garda S\xc3\xadoch\xc3\xa1na</a> (the Republic of Ireland\'s police force) colluded with the IRA in the <a href="/wiki/1989_Jonesborough_ambush" title="1989 Jonesborough ambush">killing of two senior RUC officers in 1989</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Disappeared">The Disappeared</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Troubles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: The Disappeared">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>During the 1970s and 1980s, republican and loyalist paramilitaries abducted a number of individuals, many alleged to have been informers, to be interrogated under torture and then executed.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> Eighteen people\xe2\x80\x94two women and sixteen men\xe2\x80\x94including one British Army officer, were kidnapped and killed during the Troubles. They are referred to informally as "<a href="/wiki/Disappeared_(Northern_Ireland)" title="Disappeared (Northern Ireland)">The Disappeared</a>". All but one, Lisa Dorrian, were abducted and killed by republicans. Dorrian is believed to have been abducted by loyalists. The remains of all but four of "The Disappeared" have been recovered and turned over to their families.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>British government security forces, including the <a href="/wiki/Military_Reaction_Force" title="Military Reaction Force">Military Reaction Force</a> (MRF), carried out what have been described as "<a href="/wiki/Extrajudicial_killings" class="mw-redirect" title="Extrajudicial killings">extrajudicial killings</a>" of unarmed civilians.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC1_183-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC1-183">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-II1_184-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-II1-184">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> Their victims were often Catholic or suspected Catholic civilians unaffiliated with any paramilitaries, such as 12 May 1972 <a href="/wiki/Military_Reaction_Force#Andersonstown_shootings" title="Military Reaction Force">Andersonstown shooting</a> of seven unarmed Catholic civilians and 15 April 1972 Whiterock Road shooting of two unarmed Catholic civilians by British soldiers.<sup id="cite_ref-mckittrick182_186-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mckittrick182-186">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup> A member of the MRF stated in 1978 that the Army often attempted <a href="/wiki/False_flag" title="False flag">false flag</a> sectarian attacks, thus provoking sectarian conflict and "taking the heat off the Army".<sup id="cite_ref-murray44-45_187-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-murray44-45-187">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> A former member stated that "[W]e were not there to act like an army unit, we were there to act like a terror group".<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Shoot-to-kill_allegations">Shoot-to-kill allegations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Troubles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Shoot-to-kill allegations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Shoot-to-kill_policy_in_Northern_Ireland" title="Shoot-to-kill policy in Northern Ireland">Shoot-to-kill policy in Northern Ireland</a></div>\n<p>Republicans allege that the security forces operated a shoot-to-kill policy rather than arresting IRA suspects. The security forces denied this and point out that in incidents such as the <a href="/wiki/Loughgall_ambush" title="Loughgall ambush">killing of eight IRA men</a> at <a href="/wiki/Loughgall" title="Loughgall">Loughgall</a> in 1987, the IRA members who were killed were heavily armed. Others argue that incidents such as the <a href="/wiki/Operation_Flavius" title="Operation Flavius">shooting of three unarmed IRA members</a> in <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar" title="Gibraltar">Gibraltar</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Special_Air_Service" title="Special Air Service">Special Air Service</a> ten months later confirmed suspicions among republicans, and in the British and Irish media, of a tacit British shoot-to-kill policy of suspected IRA members.<sup id="cite_ref-maxinewilliams_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-maxinewilliams-189">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Parades_issue">Parades issue</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Troubles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Parades issue">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Parades_in_Northern_Ireland" title="Parades in Northern Ireland">Parades in Northern Ireland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Drumcree_conflict" title="Drumcree conflict">Drumcree conflict</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Orangemen_parade_in_Bangor,_12_July_2010_-_geograph_-_1964645.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Orangemen_parade_in_Bangor%2C_12_July_2010_-_geograph_-_1964645.jpg/220px-Orangemen_parade_in_Bangor%2C_12_July_2010_-_geograph_-_1964645.jpg" width="220" height="155" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Orangemen_parade_in_Bangor%2C_12_July_2010_-_geograph_-_1964645.jpg/330px-Orangemen_parade_in_Bangor%2C_12_July_2010_-_geograph_-_1964645.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Orangemen_parade_in_Bangor%2C_12_July_2010_-_geograph_-_1964645.jpg/440px-Orangemen_parade_in_Bangor%2C_12_July_2010_-_geograph_-_1964645.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="451" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Orangemen_parade_in_Bangor,_12_July_2010_-_geograph_-_1964645.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Orangemen <a href="/wiki/Orange_walk" title="Orange walk">marching</a> in <a href="/wiki/Bangor,_County_Down" title="Bangor, County Down">Bangor</a> on the <a href="/wiki/The_Twelfth" title="The Twelfth">Twelfth of July</a> 2010</div></div></div>\n<p>Inter-communal tensions rise and violence often breaks out during the "marching season" when the Protestant <a href="/wiki/Orange_Institution" class="mw-redirect" title="Orange Institution">Orange Order</a> parades take place across Northern Ireland. The parades are held to commemorate <a href="/wiki/William_III_of_England" title="William III of England">William of Orange</a>\'s victory in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Boyne" title="Battle of the Boyne">Battle of the Boyne</a> in 1690, which secured the <a href="/wiki/Protestant_Ascendancy" title="Protestant Ascendancy">Protestant Ascendancy</a> and British rule in Ireland. One particular flashpoint which has caused continuous annual strife is the Garvaghy Road area in <a href="/wiki/Portadown" title="Portadown">Portadown</a>, where an Orange parade from <a href="/wiki/Drumcree_Church" title="Drumcree Church">Drumcree Church</a> passes through a mainly nationalist estate off the Garvaghy Road. This parade has now been banned indefinitely, following nationalist riots against the parade, and also loyalist counter-riots against its banning.\n</p><p>In 1995, 1996 and 1997, there were several weeks of prolonged rioting throughout Northern Ireland over the impasse at Drumcree. A number of people died in this violence, including a Catholic taxi driver, killed by the <a href="/wiki/Loyalist_Volunteer_Force" title="Loyalist Volunteer Force">Loyalist Volunteer Force</a>, and three (of four) nominally Catholic brothers (from a mixed-religion family) died when their house in <a href="/wiki/Ballymoney" title="Ballymoney">Ballymoney</a> was petrol-bombed.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Social_repercussions">Social repercussions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Troubles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Social repercussions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:RUC,_Crois.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/RUC%2C_Crois.jpg/220px-RUC%2C_Crois.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/RUC%2C_Crois.jpg/330px-RUC%2C_Crois.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/RUC%2C_Crois.jpg/440px-RUC%2C_Crois.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:RUC,_Crois.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A watchtower at a heavily fortified RUC base in <a href="/wiki/Crossmaglen" title="Crossmaglen">Crossmaglen</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Belfast_peaceline_Bombay_Street.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Belfast_peaceline_Bombay_Street.jpg/220px-Belfast_peaceline_Bombay_Street.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Belfast_peaceline_Bombay_Street.jpg/330px-Belfast_peaceline_Bombay_Street.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Belfast_peaceline_Bombay_Street.jpg/440px-Belfast_peaceline_Bombay_Street.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="683" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Belfast_peaceline_Bombay_Street.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A "<a href="/wiki/Peace_lines" title="Peace lines">peace line</a>" at the back of a house on Bombay Street, Belfast</div></div></div>\n<p>The impact of the Troubles on the ordinary people of Northern Ireland has been compared to that of the <a href="/wiki/The_Blitz" title="The Blitz">Blitz</a> on the people of London.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup> The stress resulting from bomb attacks, street disturbances, security checkpoints, and the constant military presence had the strongest effect on children and young adults.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup> There was also the fear that local paramilitaries instilled in their respective communities with the punishment beatings, "romperings", and the occasional <a href="/wiki/Tarring_and_feathering" title="Tarring and feathering">tarring and feathering</a> meted out to individuals for various purported infractions.<sup id="cite_ref-nelson126_195-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nelson126-195">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In addition to the violence and intimidation, there was chronic unemployment and a severe housing shortage. Many people were rendered homeless as a result of intimidation or having their houses burnt, and urban redevelopment played a role in the social upheaval. Belfast families faced being transferred to new, alien estates when older, decrepit districts such as <a href="/wiki/Sailortown,_Belfast" class="mw-redirect" title="Sailortown, Belfast">Sailortown</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Pound_Loney" class="mw-redirect" title="Pound Loney">Pound Loney</a> were being demolished. According to social worker and author Sarah Nelson, this new social problem of homelessness and disorientation contributed to the breakdown of the normal fabric of society, allowing for paramilitaries to exert a strong influence in certain districts.<sup id="cite_ref-nelson126_195-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nelson126-195">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup> Vandalism was also a major problem. In the 1970s there were 10,000 vandalised empty houses in Belfast alone. Most of the vandals were aged between eight and thirteen.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>According to one historian of the conflict, the stress of the Troubles engendered a breakdown in the previously strict sexual morality of Northern Ireland, resulting in a "confused hedonism" in respect of personal life.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup> In Derry, illegitimate births and alcoholism increased for women and the divorce rate rose.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup> Teenage alcoholism was also a problem, partly as a result of the drinking clubs established in both loyalist and republican areas. In many cases, there was little parental supervision of children in some of the poorer districts.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup> The Department of Health has looked at a report written in 2007 by Mike Tomlinson of <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_University_of_Belfast" class="mw-redirect" title="Queen&#39;s University of Belfast">Queen\'s University</a>, which asserted that the legacy of the Troubles has played a substantial role in the current rate of suicide in Northern Ireland.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Casualties">Casualties</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Troubles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Casualties">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Troubles_deaths_by_perpetrator.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Troubles_deaths_by_perpetrator.png/220px-Troubles_deaths_by_perpetrator.png" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Troubles_deaths_by_perpetrator.png/330px-Troubles_deaths_by_perpetrator.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Troubles_deaths_by_perpetrator.png/440px-Troubles_deaths_by_perpetrator.png 2x" data-file-width="998" data-file-height="561" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Troubles_deaths_by_perpetrator.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Responsibility for Troubles-related deaths between 1969 and 2001</div></div></div>\n<p>According to the <a href="/wiki/Conflict_Archive_on_the_Internet" title="Conflict Archive on the Internet">Conflict Archive on the Internet</a> (CAIN), 3,532 people were killed as a result of the conflict, from 1969 to 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-sutton-year_201-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sutton-year-201">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup> Of these, 3,489 were killed from 1969 to 1998.<sup id="cite_ref-sutton-year_201-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sutton-year-201">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup> According to the book <i>Lost Lives</i> (2006 edition), 3,720 people were killed as a result of the conflict, from 1966 to 2006. Of these, 3,635 were killed from 1969 to 1998.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup> There are reports that 257 of the victims were children under the age of seventeen, representing 7.2% of all the total during this period.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup> Other reports state that a total of 274 children under the age of eighteen were killed during the conflict.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In <i>The Politics of Antagonism: Understanding Northern Ireland</i>, Brendan O\'Leary and John McGarry point out that "nearly two per cent of the population of Northern Ireland have been killed or injured through political violence [...] If the equivalent ratio of victims to population had been produced in Great Britain in the same period some 100,000 people would have died, and if a similar level of political violence had taken place, the number of fatalities in the USA would have been over 500,000".<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup> Using this relative comparison to the US, analyst John M. Gates suggests that whatever one calls the conflict, it was "certainly not" a "<a href="/wiki/Low_intensity_conflict" title="Low intensity conflict">low intensity conflict</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2010 it was estimated that 107,000 people in Northern Ireland suffered some physical injury as a result of the conflict. On the basis of data gathered by the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_Statistics_and_Research_Agency" title="Northern Ireland Statistics and Research Agency">Northern Ireland Statistics and Research Agency</a>, the Victims Commission estimated that the conflict resulted in 500,000 \'victims\' in Northern Ireland alone. It defines \'victims\' are those who are directly affected by \'bereavement\', \'physical injury\' or \'trauma\' as a result of the conflict.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Responsibility">Responsibility</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Troubles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Responsibility">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Approximately 60% of the dead were killed by republicans, 30% by loyalists and 10% by British security forces.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" style="width:400px; margin: 0 auto;">\n<caption>Responsibility for killing<sup id="cite_ref-suttonresponsible_208-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-suttonresponsible-208">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup>\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th scope="col">Responsible party\n</th>\n<th scope="col">No.\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Republican paramilitary groups\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">2058\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Loyalist paramilitary groups\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">1027\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>British security forces\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">363\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Persons unknown\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">79\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Irish security forces\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">5\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><b>Total</b>\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;"><b>3532</b>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>According to Malcolm Sutton\'s <i>Index of Deaths from the Conflict in Ireland</i>:<sup id="cite_ref-org-status_209-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-org-status-209">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Of those killed by British security forces:\n</p>\n<ul><li>187 (~51.5%) were civilians</li>\n<li>145 (~39.9%) were members of republican paramilitaries</li>\n<li>18 (~4.9%) were members of loyalist paramilitaries</li>\n<li>13 (~3.5%) were fellow members of the British security forces</li></ul>\n<p>Of those killed by republican paramilitaries:\n</p>\n<ul><li>1080 (~52%) were members/former members of the British security forces</li>\n<li>723 (~35%) were civilians</li>\n<li>187 (~9%) were members of republican paramilitaries</li>\n<li>57 (~2.7%) were members of loyalist paramilitaries</li>\n<li>11 (~0.5%) were members of the <a href="/wiki/Irish_security_forces" title="Irish security forces">Irish security forces</a></li></ul>\n<p>Of those killed by loyalist paramilitaries:\n</p>\n<ul><li>878 (~85.4%) were civilians</li>\n<li>94 (~9%) were members of loyalist paramilitaries</li>\n<li>41 (~4%) were members of republican paramilitaries</li>\n<li>14 (~1%) were members of the British security forces</li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Status">Status</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Troubles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Status">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Approximately 52% of the dead were civilians, 32% were members/former members of the British security forces, 11% were members of republican paramilitaries, and 5% were members of loyalist paramilitaries.<sup id="cite_ref-suttonresponsible_208-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-suttonresponsible-208">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup> About 60% of the civilian casualties were Catholics, 30% were Protestants, and the rest were from outside Northern Ireland.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Of the civilian casualties, 48% were killed by loyalists, 39% were killed by republicans, and 10% were killed by the British security forces.<sup id="cite_ref-org-status_209-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-org-status-209">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>It has been the subject of dispute whether some individuals were members of paramilitary organisations due to their secretive nature. Several casualties that were listed as civilians were later claimed by the IRA as their members.<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup> One <a href="/wiki/Ulster_Defence_Association" title="Ulster Defence Association">Ulster Defence Association</a> (UDA) and three <a href="/wiki/Ulster_Volunteer_Force" title="Ulster Volunteer Force">Ulster Volunteer Force</a> (UVF) members killed during the conflict were also <a href="/wiki/Ulster_Defence_Regiment" title="Ulster Defence Regiment">Ulster Defence Regiment</a> (UDR) soldiers at the time of their deaths.<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup> At least one civilian victim was an off-duty member of the <a href="/wiki/Territorial_Army_(United_Kingdom)" class="mw-redirect" title="Territorial Army (United Kingdom)">Territorial Army</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" style="width:400px; margin:0 auto;">\n<caption>Deaths by status of victim<sup id="cite_ref-suttonstatus_7-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-suttonstatus-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th scope="col">Status\n</th>\n<th scope="col">No.\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Civilians <small>(inc. Civilian political activists)</small>\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">1841\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>British security force personnel <small>(serving and former members)</small>\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">1114\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="padding-left: 2em;"><a href="/wiki/British_Army" title="British Army">British Army</a> (inc. <a href="/wiki/Ulster_Defence_Regiment" title="Ulster Defence Regiment">UDR</a>, <a href="/wiki/Royal_Irish_Regiment_(1992)" title="Royal Irish Regiment (1992)">RIR</a> and <a href="/wiki/Territorial_Army_(United_Kingdom)" class="mw-redirect" title="Territorial Army (United Kingdom)">TA</a>)\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">757\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="padding-left: 2em;"><a id="Location">Location</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Troubles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Location">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Deaths_in_The_Troubles_by_area.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Deaths_in_The_Troubles_by_area.png/220px-Deaths_in_The_Troubles_by_area.png" width="220" height="196" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Deaths_in_The_Troubles_by_area.png/330px-Deaths_in_The_Troubles_by_area.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Deaths_in_The_Troubles_by_area.png/440px-Deaths_in_The_Troubles_by_area.png 2x" data-file-width="447" data-file-height="399" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Deaths_in_The_Troubles_by_area.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Troubles deaths by area</div></div></div>\n<p>Most killings took place within Northern Ireland, especially in Belfast. Most of the killings in Belfast took place in the west and north of the city. <a href="/wiki/Dublin" title="Dublin">Dublin</a>, London and <a href="/wiki/Birmingham" title="Birmingham">Birmingham</a> were also affected, albeit to a lesser degree than Northern Ireland itself. Occasionally, the IRA attempted or carried out attacks on British targets in Gibraltar, Germany and the Netherlands.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" style="width:400px; margin: 0 auto;">\n<caption>Conflict-related deaths by location<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup>\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Troubles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">\n<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-39"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-39">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The "troubles" was used to describe the 17th century <a href="/wiki/Wars_of_the_Three_Kingdoms" title="Wars of the Three Kingdoms">Wars of the Three Kingdoms</a> by all three national parliaments. For example, after the <a href="/wiki/Restoration_(1660)" title="Restoration (1660)">Restoration</a> in 1660 the English <i><a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/An_act_of_free_and_general_pardon,_indemnity_and_oblivion" class="extiw" title="s:An act of free and general pardon, indemnity and oblivion">Act of free and general pardon, indemnity and oblivion</a></i> starts with "The King\'s most excellent Majesty, taking into his gracious and serious consideration the long and great troubles..."; as does the similar act in Scotland: "The king\'s most excellent majesty, considering that by the late troubles diverse of his subjects..." (<a href="#CITEREFScottish_Parliament1662">Scottish Parliament 1662</a>); and by the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Ireland" title="Parliament of Ireland">Irish Parliament</a> to describe the same period in <i>An Act for the Conformation of Marriages</i> (12 C. 2, 33 Eng.): "...marriages since the beginning of the late troubles..." (<a href="#CITEREFIrish_Parliament1794">Irish Parliament 1794</a>, p.&#160;137).</span>\n</li>\n</ol></div></div>\n<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">\n<div class="mw-references-wrap mw-references-columns"><ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://cain.ulst.ac.uk/faq/faq2.htm">Frequently Asked Questions \xe2\x80\x93 The Northern Ireland Conflict</a>, cain.ulst.ac.uk.
